					<div id="mw-content-text" class="mw-body-content"><div class="mw-content-ltr mw-parser-output" lang="en" dir="ltr"><div class="shortdescription nomobile noexcerpt noprint searchaux" style="display:none">Small citrus fruit</div>
<p class="mw-empty-elt">

</p>

<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align: center"><b><span class="binomial"><span style="font-weight:normal;"></span><i>Citrus reticulata</i></span></b><br /><div style="font-size: 85%;"><a href="/wiki/Francisco_Manuel_Blanco" class="mw-redirect" title="Francisco Manuel Blanco">Blanco</a>, 1837</div>
</td></tr>


































</tbody></table><style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1220493105">html.skin-theme-clientpref-night .mw-parser-output .infobox.biota tr{background:transparent!important}html.skin-theme-clientpref-night .mw-parser-output .infobox.biota img{background:white}@media(prefers-color-scheme:dark){html.skin-theme-clientpref-os .mw-parser-output .infobox.biota tr{background:transparent!important}html.skin-theme-clientpref-os .mw-parser-output .infobox.biota img{background:white}}</style>
<p>The <b>mandarin orange</b> (<i><b>Citrus reticulata</b></i>), also known as <b>mandarin</b> or <b>mandarine</b>, is a small, rounded <a href="/wiki/Citrus" title="Citrus">citrus</a> tree <a href="/wiki/Fruit" title="Fruit">fruit</a>. Treated as a distinct species of <a href="/wiki/Orange_(fruit)" title="Orange (fruit)">orange</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-morton_1-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-morton-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> it is usually eaten plain or in fruit salads.<sup id="cite_ref-morton_1-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-morton-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Tangerine" title="Tangerine">Tangerines</a> are a group of orange-colored citrus fruit consisting of hybrids of mandarin orange with some <a href="/wiki/Pomelo" title="Pomelo">pomelo</a> contribution.
</p><p>Mandarins are smaller and oblate,<sup id="cite_ref-morton_1-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-morton-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> unlike the <a href="/wiki/Spherical" class="mw-redirect" title="Spherical">spherical</a> common <a href="/wiki/Orange_(fruit)" title="Orange (fruit)">oranges</a> (which are a mandarin–<a href="/wiki/Pomelo" title="Pomelo">pomelo</a> <a href="/wiki/Hybrid_(biology)" title="Hybrid (biology)">hybrid</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-Talon_2-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Talon-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup>   The <a href="/wiki/Taste" title="Taste">taste</a> is considered sweeter and stronger than the common orange.<sup id="cite_ref-karp_3-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-karp-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> A ripe mandarin is firm to slightly soft, heavy for its size, and pebbly-skinned. The peel is thin, loose,<sup id="cite_ref-morton_1-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-morton-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> with little white <a href="/wiki/Mesocarp" class="mw-redirect" title="Mesocarp">mesocarp</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-latimes_4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-latimes-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> so they are usually easier to peel and to split into segments.<sup id="cite_ref-morton_1-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-morton-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> Hybrids usually have these traits to a lesser degree. The mandarin is tender and is damaged easily by cold. It can be grown in tropical and subtropical areas.<sup id="cite_ref-morton_1-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-morton-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-karp_3-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-karp-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>According to genetic studies, the mandarin was one of the <a href="/wiki/Citrus_taxonomy#Ancestral_species" title="Citrus taxonomy">original citrus species</a>; through breeding or natural hybridization, it is the ancestor of many <a href="/wiki/Citrus_taxonomy#Hybrids" title="Citrus taxonomy">hybrid citrus</a> cultivars. With the <a href="/wiki/Citron" title="Citron">citron</a> and pomelo, it is the ancestor of the most commercially important hybrids (such as sweet and sour oranges, grapefruit, and many lemons and limes). The mandarin has also been hybridized with other citrus species, such as the <a href="/wiki/Desert_lime" class="mw-redirect" title="Desert lime">desert lime</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Kumquat" title="Kumquat">kumquat</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Talon_2-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Talon-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> Though the ancestral mandarin was bitter, most commercial mandarin strains derive from hybridization with pomelo, which gives them a sweet fruit.<sup id="cite_ref-Wang_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Wang-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<meta property="mw:PageProp/toc" />
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">Etymology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mandarin_orange&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Etymology"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The name <i>mandarin orange</i> is a <a href="/wiki/Calque" title="Calque">calque</a> of Swedish <i>mandarin apelsin</i> [<i>apelsin</i> from German <i>Apfelsine</i> (<i>Apfel</i> + <i><a href="/wiki/Names_of_china" class="mw-redirect" title="Names of china">Sina</a></i>), meaning <i>Chinese apple</i>], first attested in the 18th century. The Imperial Chinese term "mandarine" was first adopted by the <a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">French</a> for this fruit. The reason for the epithet is not clear.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><i>Citrus reticulata</i> is from Latin, where reticulata means "netted".<sup id="cite_ref-mbg_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mbg-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Botany">Botany</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mandarin_orange&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Botany"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Mandarinier_Gortyne.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Mandarinier_Gortyne.jpg/220px-Mandarinier_Gortyne.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="254" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Mandarinier_Gortyne.jpg/330px-Mandarinier_Gortyne.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Mandarinier_Gortyne.jpg/440px-Mandarinier_Gortyne.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2880" data-file-height="3330" /></a><figcaption>Mandarin oranges growing on a tree in <a href="/wiki/Crete" title="Crete">Crete</a>.</figcaption></figure>
<p><i>Citrus reticulata</i> is a moderate-sized tree some 7.6 metres (25&#160;ft) in height.<sup id="cite_ref-morton_1-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-morton-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-mbg_7-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mbg-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> The tree trunk and major branches have thorns.<sup id="cite_ref-morton_1-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-morton-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> The leaves are shiny, green, and rather small.<sup id="cite_ref-morton_1-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-morton-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Petiole_(botany)" title="Petiole (botany)">petioles</a> are short, almost wingless or slightly winged.<sup id="cite_ref-morton_1-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-morton-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> The flowers are borne singly or in small groups in the leaf-axils.<sup id="cite_ref-morton_1-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-morton-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> Citrus are usually <a href="/wiki/Self-fertile" class="mw-redirect" title="Self-fertile">self-fertile</a> (needing only a <a href="/wiki/Bee" title="Bee">bee</a> to move <a href="/wiki/Pollen" title="Pollen">pollen</a> within the same flower) or <a href="/wiki/Parthenocarpic" class="mw-redirect" title="Parthenocarpic">parthenocarpic</a> (not needing <a href="/wiki/Pollination" title="Pollination">pollination</a> and therefore seedless, such as the <a href="/wiki/Satsuma_(fruit)" class="mw-redirect" title="Satsuma (fruit)">satsuma</a>). A mature mandarin tree can yield up to 79 kilograms (175&#160;lb) of fruit.<sup id="cite_ref-ucr_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ucr-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Fruit">Fruit</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mandarin_orange&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Fruit"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Mandarin_oranges_in_mesh_bag.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/Mandarin_oranges_in_mesh_bag.jpg/220px-Mandarin_oranges_in_mesh_bag.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/Mandarin_oranges_in_mesh_bag.jpg/330px-Mandarin_oranges_in_mesh_bag.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/Mandarin_oranges_in_mesh_bag.jpg/440px-Mandarin_oranges_in_mesh_bag.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4032" data-file-height="3024" /></a><figcaption>Mandarin oranges in a mesh bag</figcaption></figure>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Mandarin_orange_seeds.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Mandarin_orange_seeds.jpg/220px-Mandarin_orange_seeds.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="242" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Mandarin_orange_seeds.jpg/330px-Mandarin_orange_seeds.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Mandarin_orange_seeds.jpg/440px-Mandarin_orange_seeds.jpg 2x" data-file-width="585" data-file-height="644" /></a><figcaption>Mandarin orange seeds</figcaption></figure>
<p>Mandarin orange fruits are small 40–80 millimetres (1.6–3.1&#160;in).<sup id="cite_ref-morton_1-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-morton-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> Their color is <a href="/wiki/Orange_(colour)" title="Orange (colour)">orange</a>, yellow-orange, or red-orange.<sup id="cite_ref-karp_3-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-karp-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> The skin is thin and peels off easily.<sup id="cite_ref-morton_1-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-morton-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> Their easiness to peel is an important advantage of mandarin oranges over other citrus fruits.<sup id="cite_ref-karp_3-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-karp-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> Just like with other citrus fruits, mandarin is separated easily from the segments.<sup id="cite_ref-morton_1-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-morton-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> The fruits may be <a href="/wiki/Seedless" class="mw-redirect" title="Seedless">seedless</a> or contain a small number of <a href="/wiki/Seed" title="Seed">seeds</a>. Mandarin orange fruits are <a href="/wiki/Sweetness" title="Sweetness">sweet</a> to taste and can be eaten as whole or squeezed to make <a href="/wiki/Juice" title="Juice">juice</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-morton_1-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-morton-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-karp_3-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-karp-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Production">Production</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mandarin_orange&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Production"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>In 2022, world production of mandarin oranges (combined with tangerines, clementines, and satsumas in reporting to <a href="/wiki/FAOSTAT" class="mw-redirect" title="FAOSTAT">FAOSTAT</a>) was 44.2 million <a href="/wiki/Tonne" title="Tonne">tonnes</a>, led by China with 61% of the global total.<sup id="cite_ref-faostat_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-faostat-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> Spain produced 1.8 million tonnes in 2022, with <a href="/wiki/Turkey" title="Turkey">Turkey</a>, <a href="/wiki/Egypt" title="Egypt">Egypt</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Morocco" title="Morocco">Morocco</a> as other significant producers.<sup id="cite_ref-faostat_9-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-faostat-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Uses">Uses</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mandarin_orange&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Uses"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Culinary">Culinary</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mandarin_orange&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Culinary"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Fresh">Fresh</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mandarin_orange&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Fresh"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1033289096">.mw-parser-output .hatnote{font-style:italic}.mw-parser-output div.hatnote{padding-left:1.6em;margin-bottom:0.5em}.mw-parser-output .hatnote i{font-style:normal}.mw-parser-output .hatnote+link+.hatnote{margin-top:-0.5em}</style><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_fruit_dishes" title="List of fruit dishes">List of fruit dishes</a></div>
<p>Mandarins are generally peeled and eaten fresh or used in salads, desserts and main dishes.<sup id="cite_ref-morton_1-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-morton-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> Fresh mandarin juice and frozen juice concentrate are commonly available in the United States. The number of seeds in each segment (carpel) varies greatly. Fresh mandarins are also used in the production of some drinks and spirits, such as <a href="/wiki/Mandarine_Napol%C3%A9on" title="Mandarine Napoléon">Mandarine Napoléon</a>.
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Peel">Peel</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mandarin_orange&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Peel"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Peel_(fruit)" title="Peel (fruit)">peel</a> is used fresh, whole or <a href="/wiki/Zest_(ingredient)" title="Zest (ingredient)">zested</a>, or dried as <a href="/wiki/Chenpi" title="Chenpi">chenpi</a>. It can be used as a spice for cooking, baking, drinks, or candy. <a href="/wiki/Essential_oil" title="Essential oil">Essential oil</a> from the fresh peel may be used as a flavouring for candy, in <a href="/wiki/Gelatin" title="Gelatin">gelatins</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ice_cream" title="Ice cream">ice cream</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chewing_gum" title="Chewing gum">chewing gum</a>, and baked goods.<sup id="cite_ref-morton_1-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-morton-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> It is also used as a flavouring in <a href="/wiki/Liqueur" title="Liqueur">liqueurs</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-morton_1-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-morton-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> In <a href="/wiki/Chinese_cuisine" title="Chinese cuisine">Chinese cuisine</a>, the peel of the mandarin orange, called chenpi, is used to flavor sweet dishes and sauces.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2021)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Canning">Canning</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mandarin_orange&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Canning"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Canned mandarin segments are peeled to remove the white pith before canning; otherwise, they turn bitter. Segments are peeled using a chemical process. First, the segments are scalded in hot water to loosen the skin; then, they are bathed in a <a href="/wiki/Lye" title="Lye">lye</a> solution, which digests the <a href="/wiki/Mesocarp" class="mw-redirect" title="Mesocarp">albedo</a> and membranes. Finally, the segments are rinsed several times in plain water. Once orange segments are properly prepared, mandarin oranges undergo heat processing to remove bacteria that can cause spoilage. The oranges are then packed in airtight sealed containers. Ascorbic acid may also be added.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2022)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p>

</td></tr><tr><td colspan="2" class="infobox-full-data"><hr /><div class="wrap" style="padding:0.3em;line-height:1.2em;"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20150704005654/http://ndb.nal.usda.gov/ndb/search/list?qlookup=09218&amp;format=Full">Link to USDA Database entry</a></div></td></tr><tr><td colspan="2" class="infobox-below wrap" style="background:#e0e0e0;padding:0.3em;line-height:1.5em;font-weight:normal;"><sup>†</sup>Percentages estimated using <a href="/wiki/Reference_Daily_Intake#Daily_Values" title="Reference Daily Intake">US&#160;recommendations</a> for adults,<sup id="cite_ref-FDADailyValues_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FDADailyValues-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> except for potassium, which is estimated based on expert recommendation from <a href="/wiki/National_Academies_of_Sciences,_Engineering,_and_Medicine" title="National Academies of Sciences, Engineering, and Medicine">the National Academies</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-NationalAcademiesPotassium_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NationalAcademiesPotassium-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>A mandarin orange contains 85% water, 13% <a href="/wiki/Carbohydrate" title="Carbohydrate">carbohydrates</a>, and negligible amounts of <a href="/wiki/Fat" title="Fat">fat</a> and <a href="/wiki/Protein" title="Protein">protein</a> (table). Among <a href="/wiki/Micronutrient" title="Micronutrient">micronutrients</a>, only <a href="/wiki/Vitamin_C" title="Vitamin C">vitamin C</a> is in significant content (32% of the <a href="/wiki/Daily_Value" class="mw-redirect" title="Daily Value">Daily Value</a>) in a 100-gram reference serving, with all other nutrients in low amounts.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Cultural_significance">Cultural significance</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mandarin_orange&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Cultural significance"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Citrus_reticulata_Fruchtansatz.JPG" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/Citrus_reticulata_Fruchtansatz.JPG/170px-Citrus_reticulata_Fruchtansatz.JPG" decoding="async" width="170" height="227" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/Citrus_reticulata_Fruchtansatz.JPG/255px-Citrus_reticulata_Fruchtansatz.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/Citrus_reticulata_Fruchtansatz.JPG/340px-Citrus_reticulata_Fruchtansatz.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2592" data-file-height="3456" /></a><figcaption>Mandarin fruitlets</figcaption></figure>
<p>In Canada and the United States, they are commonly purchased in 5- or 10-pound boxes,<sup id="cite_ref-karp_3-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-karp-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> individually wrapped in soft green paper, and given in <a href="/wiki/Christmas_stocking" title="Christmas stocking">Christmas stockings</a>. This custom goes back to the 1880s when Japanese immigrants in Canada and the United States began receiving Japanese mandarin oranges from their families back home as gifts for the New Year. The tradition spread among the non-Japanese population and eastwards across the country: each November harvest, "The oranges were quickly unloaded and shipped east by rail. 'Orange Trains' – trains with boxcars painted orange – alerted everyone along the way that the irresistible oranges from Japan were back again for the holidays. For many, the arrival of Japanese mandarin oranges signalled the beginning of the holiday season."<sup id="cite_ref-AITC1_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AITC1-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> This Japanese tradition merged with European traditions related to the <a href="/wiki/Christmas_stocking" title="Christmas stocking">Christmas stocking</a>. <a href="/wiki/Saint_Nicholas" title="Saint Nicholas">Saint Nicholas</a> is said to have put <a href="/wiki/Gold" title="Gold">gold</a> coins into the stockings of three poor girls so that they would be able to afford to get married.<sup id="cite_ref-AFP_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AFP-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> Sometimes the story is told with gold balls instead of bags of gold, and oranges became a symbolic stand-in for these gold balls, and are put in Christmas stockings in Canada<sup id="cite_ref-AFP_13-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AFP-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Marion_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Marion-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> along with <a href="/wiki/Chocolate_coins" class="mw-redirect" title="Chocolate coins">chocolate coins</a> wrapped in gold foil.
</p><p>Satsumas were also grown in the United States from the early 1900s. Still, Japan remained a major supplier.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> U.S. imports of these Japanese oranges was suspended due to hostilities with Japan during World War II.<sup id="cite_ref-AITC1_12-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AITC1-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> While they were one of the first Japanese goods allowed for export after the end of the war, residual hostility led to the rebranding of these oranges as "Mandarin" oranges instead of "Japanese" oranges.<sup id="cite_ref-AITC1_12-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AITC1-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The delivery of the first batch of mandarin oranges from Japan in the port of <a href="/wiki/Vancouver" title="Vancouver">Vancouver, British Columbia</a> (Canada) is greeted with a festival that combines Santa Claus and Japanese dancers<sup id="cite_ref-Marion_14-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Marion-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup>—young girls dressed in traditional <a href="/wiki/Kimono" title="Kimono">kimono</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-France-CanadaChristmas_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-France-CanadaChristmas-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Historically, the Christmas fruit sold in North America was mostly <a href="/wiki/Dancy_(fruit)" class="mw-redirect" title="Dancy (fruit)">Dancys</a>, but now it is more often a hybrid.<sup id="cite_ref-arkoftaste_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-arkoftaste-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Literature">Literature</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mandarin_orange&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Literature"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In Canadian literature, particularly in <a href="/wiki/Gabrielle_Roy" title="Gabrielle Roy">Gabrielle Roy</a>'s novel about <a href="/wiki/Montreal" title="Montreal">Montreal</a>, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Tin_Flute" title="The Tin Flute">The Tin Flute</a></i>, a mandarin orange figures as a  touch of luxury for the dying son of the poor Lacasse family, around which the novel is woven.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2021)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> Mandarin oranges are mentioned in  <a href="/wiki/Sinclair_Ross" title="Sinclair Ross">Sinclair Ross</a>' 1942 novel, <i><a href="/wiki/As_for_Me_and_My_House" title="As for Me and My House">As for Me and My House</a></i>, and his 1939 short story, <i>Cornet at Night</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Genetics_and_origin">Genetics and origin</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mandarin_orange&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Genetics and origin"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Citrus_taxonomy" title="Citrus taxonomy">Citrus taxonomy</a></div>
<p>Mandarins are one of the pure ancestral citrus <a href="/wiki/Taxa" class="mw-redirect" title="Taxa">taxa</a>, and are thought to have evolved in regions including <a href="/wiki/South_China" title="South China">South China</a> and Japan in <a href="/wiki/East_Asia" title="East Asia">East Asia</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Vietnam" title="Vietnam">Vietnam</a> in <a href="/wiki/Southeast_Asia" title="Southeast Asia">Southeast Asia</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Curk_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Curk-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Wang_5-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Wang-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup>  Mandarins appear to have been domesticated at least twice, in the north and south <a href="/wiki/Nanling_Mountains" title="Nanling Mountains">Nanling Mountains</a>, derived from separate wild subspecies.  Wild mandarins are still found there, including Daoxian mandarines (sometimes given the species name <i>Citrus daoxianensis</i>) as well as some members of the group traditionally called 'Mangshan wild mandarins', a generic grouping for the wild mandarin-like fruit of the Mangshan area that includes both true mandarins (<i>mangshanyeju</i>,<sup id="cite_ref-Wu2021_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Wu2021-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> the southern subspecies) and the genetically distinct and only distantly-related <a href="/wiki/Mangshanyegan" class="mw-redirect" title="Mangshanyegan">Mangshanyegan</a>. The wild mandarins were found free of the introgressed pomelo (<i>C. maxima</i>) DNA found in domestic mandarins. Still, they did appear to have small amounts (~1.8%) of introgression from the <a href="/wiki/Citrus_ichangensis" class="mw-redirect" title="Citrus ichangensis">ichang papeda</a>, which grows wild in the same region.<sup id="cite_ref-Wang2018_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Wang2018-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The Nanling Mountains are also home to northern and southern genetic clusters of domestic mandarins that have similar levels of sugars in the fruit compared to their wild relatives but appreciably (in some almost 90-fold) lower levels of citric acid.  The clusters display different patterns of pomelo introgression, have different deduced historical population histories, and are most closely related to distinct wild mandarins, suggesting two independent domestications in the north and south.<sup id="cite_ref-Wang2018_21-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Wang2018-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup>  All tested domesticated cultivars were found to belong to one of these two genetic clusters, with varieties such as Nanfengmiju, Kishu and Satsuma deriving from the northern domestication event producing larger, redder fruit, while Willowleaf, Dancy, Sunki, Cleopatra, King, Ponkan, and others derived from the smaller, yellower-fruited southern cluster.<sup id="cite_ref-Wang2018_21-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Wang2018-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Citrus_taxonomy" title="Citrus taxonomy">Tanaka classification system</a> divided domestic mandarins and similar fruit into numerous species, giving distinct names to cultivars such as willowleaf mandarins (<i>C. deliciosa</i>), <a href="/wiki/Satsuma_(fruit)" class="mw-redirect" title="Satsuma (fruit)">satsumas</a> (<i>C. unshiu</i>), <a href="/wiki/Tangerines" class="mw-redirect" title="Tangerines">tangerines</a> (<i>C. tangerina</i>). Under the <a href="/wiki/Citrus_taxonomy" title="Citrus taxonomy">Swingle system</a>, all these are considered to be varieties of a single species, <i>Citrus reticulata</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-identification_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-identification-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup>  Hodgson represented them as several subgroups: common (<i>C. reticulata</i>), Satsuma, <a href="/wiki/Citrus_nobilis" class="mw-redirect" title="Citrus nobilis">King</a> (<i>C. nobilis</i>), Mediterranean (willowleaf), small-fruited (<i>C. indica</i>, <i>C. tachibana</i> and <i>C. reshni</i>), and mandarin hybrids.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> In the genomic-based species taxonomy of Ollitrault et al., only pure mandarins would fall under <i>C. reticulata</i>, while the pomelo admixture found in the majority of mandarins would cause them to be classified as varieties of <i>C. aurantium</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Genetic analysis is consistent with continental mandarins representing a single species, with much of the variation within mandarins being due to hybridization.<sup id="cite_ref-Talon_2-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Talon-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> A separate species, <i><a href="/wiki/Citrus_ryukyuensis" title="Citrus ryukyuensis">Citrus ryukyuensis</a></i> that diverged from the mainland species between 2 and 3 million years ago when cut off by rising sea levals was found growing on the island of <a href="/wiki/Okinawa" class="mw-redirect" title="Okinawa">Okinawa</a>, and its natural and agricultural hybridization with the mainland mandarin species has produced some of the unique island mandarin cultivars of Japan and Taiwan, such as the <a href="/wiki/Tachibana_orange" title="Tachibana orange">Tachibana orange</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Wu2021_20-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Wu2021-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> previously classified as a subspecies of pure mandarin<sup id="cite_ref-Talon_2-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Talon-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> before its parent was identified, and the <a href="/wiki/Shekwasha" class="mw-redirect" title="Shekwasha">Shekwasha</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Wu2021_20-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Wu2021-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> Some of the small number of cultivars were found to be pure in initial gemonic analysis, including <a href="/w/index.php?title=Sun_Chu_Sha_mandarin&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Sun Chu Sha mandarin (page does not exist)">Sun Chu Sha mandarin</a><sup id="cite_ref-Curk_19-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Curk-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Talon_2-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Talon-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Nanfengmiju" title="Nanfengmiju">Nanfengmiju</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-auto_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> but Wang detected in them not only an apparent Ichang papeda introgression found in all examined mandarins but also the distinct pomelo DNA of the domesticated mandarins.<sup id="cite_ref-Wang2018_21-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Wang2018-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> Following initial hybridization, natural or cultivated backcrosses of the initial mandarin-pomelo hybrids with the mandarin stock produced mandarins with limited pomelo contribution,<sup id="cite_ref-Talon_2-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Talon-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> that differed between the northern and southern domesticates.<sup id="cite_ref-Wang2018_21-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Wang2018-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup>  An 'acidic' group of cultivars including <a href="/w/index.php?title=Sunki_mandarin&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Sunki mandarin (page does not exist)">Sunki</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cleopatra_mandarin" class="mw-redirect" title="Cleopatra mandarin">Cleopatra mandarins</a> that likewise previously were thought to be pure but since found to contain small regions of <a href="/wiki/Introgression" title="Introgression">introgressed</a> pomelo DNA are too sour to be edible, but are widely used as rootstock and grown for juice.<sup id="cite_ref-identification_22-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-identification-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Talon_2-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Talon-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup>  Another group of mandarins, including some tangerines, Satsuma and King mandarins, show a greater pomelo contribution and derive from the limited-pomelo hybrids being crossed again, with sweet orange or pomelo, and likewise backcrossing in some cases, producing cultivars with moderate to high levels of pomelo introgression.<sup id="cite_ref-Talon_2-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Talon-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup>  Hybrid mandarins thus fall on a continuum of increasing pomelo contribution with clementines, sweet and sour oranges, and grapefruit.<sup id="cite_ref-Curk_19-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Curk-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup>  Mandarins and their hybrids are sold under a variety of names.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Varieties">Varieties</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mandarin_orange&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Varieties"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Citrus_taxonomy" title="Citrus taxonomy">Citrus taxonomy</a></div>

<h3><span id="Stem_mandarins_.28Citrus_reticulata.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Stem_mandarins_(Citrus_reticulata)">Stem mandarins (Citrus reticulata)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mandarin_orange&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Stem mandarins (Citrus reticulata)"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul><li>Mangshan wild mandarins (only some, others being the genetically distinct mangshanyegan)<sup id="cite_ref-Wang2018_21-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Wang2018-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>Daoxian mandarines<sup id="cite_ref-Wang2018_21-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Wang2018-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>Suanpangan<sup id="cite_ref-Wang2018_21-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Wang2018-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Domesticated_mandarins_and_hybrids">Domesticated mandarins and hybrids</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mandarin_orange&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Domesticated mandarins and hybrids"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>(Species names are those from the Tanaka system. Recent genomic analysis would place them all in <i>Citrus reticulata</i>,<sup id="cite_ref-Talon_2-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Talon-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> except the <i>C. ryukyuensis</i> hybrids<sup id="cite_ref-Wu2021_20-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Wu2021-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup>)
</p>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Harvest_Kinnow.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c9/Harvest_Kinnow.jpg/220px-Harvest_Kinnow.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c9/Harvest_Kinnow.jpg/330px-Harvest_Kinnow.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c9/Harvest_Kinnow.jpg/440px-Harvest_Kinnow.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2048" data-file-height="1536" /></a><figcaption><a href="/wiki/Kinnow" title="Kinnow">Kinnow</a>, a 'King' (<a href="/wiki/Citrus_nobilis" class="mw-redirect" title="Citrus nobilis">Citrus nobilis</a>) × 'Willow Leaf' (<a href="/wiki/Citrus_%C3%97_deliciosa" title="Citrus × deliciosa">Citrus × deliciosa</a>) cross, developed by Dr H.B. Frost</figcaption></figure>
<ul><li><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sun_Chu_Sha_mandarin&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Sun Chu Sha mandarin (page does not exist)">Sun Chu Sha</a><sup id="cite_ref-Curk_19-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Curk-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Talon_2-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Talon-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Nanfengmiju" title="Nanfengmiju">Nanfengmiju</a> - one of China's most widely cultivated varieties.<sup id="cite_ref-auto_25-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Cleopatra_mandarin" class="mw-redirect" title="Cleopatra mandarin">Cleopatra mandarin</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Curk_19-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Curk-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> acidic mandarin containing very small amount of pomelo <a href="/wiki/Introgression" title="Introgression">introgression</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Talon_2-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Talon-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sunki_mandarin&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Sunki mandarin (page does not exist)">Sunki</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Curk_19-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Curk-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> acidic mandarin containing very small amount of pomelo <a href="/wiki/Introgression" title="Introgression">introgression</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Talon_2-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Talon-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Tangerine" title="Tangerine">Tangerines</a> (<i>Citrus tangerina</i>)<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> is a grouping used for several distinct mandarin hybrids.  Those sold in the US as tangerines have usually been <a href="/wiki/Dancy_(fruit)" class="mw-redirect" title="Dancy (fruit)">Dancy</a>, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Sunburst_(fruit)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Sunburst (fruit) (page does not exist)">Sunburst</a> or <a href="/wiki/Murcott_(fruit)" title="Murcott (fruit)">Murcott</a> (Honey) cultivars.  Some tangerine × grapefruit hybrids are legally sold as tangerines in the US.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-florida.eregulations.us_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-florida.eregulations.us-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>Mediterranean/Willowleaf/Thorny (<i><a href="/wiki/Citrus_%C3%97_deliciosa" title="Citrus × deliciosa">Citrus × deliciosa</a></i>), a mandarin with small amounts of pomelo.<sup id="cite_ref-genealogy_review_29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-genealogy_review-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>Dalanghita (<i>Citrus reticulata</i>) is a smaller mandarin endemic widely cultivated in the Philippines. Also known by other local names, <i>naranghita</i> and <i>sintones</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/w/index.php?title=Huanglingmiao&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Huanglingmiao (page does not exist)">Huanglingmiao</a> (<i>Citrus reticulata</i>), a mandarin–pomelo hybrid.<sup id="cite_ref-Talon_2-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Talon-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-genealogy_31-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-genealogy-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Kishumikan" class="mw-redirect" title="Kishumikan">Kishumikan</a> (<i>Citrus reticulata</i>), or simply Kishu, a close clonal relative of Huanglingmiao, the two sharing a common origin before diverging as they were propagated<sup id="cite_ref-Talon_2-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Talon-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup>
<ul><li><a href="/w/index.php?title=Kunenbo&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Kunenbo (page does not exist)">Kunenbo</a> (<i>Citrus nobilis</i>) a heterogeneous group that includes at least four distinct mandarin-pomelo hybrids.<sup id="cite_ref-Shimizu_32-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Shimizu-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Cam_s%C3%A0nh" title="Cam sành">King</a> (in full, 'King of Siam', <i>Citrus nobilis</i>) a Kunenbo mandarin with high levels of pomelo admixture, sometimes classed as a tangor.<sup id="cite_ref-Talon_2-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Talon-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Shimizu_32-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Shimizu-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Kinnow" title="Kinnow">Kinnow</a> (see image), a King × Willowleaf hybrid.</li></ul></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Citrus_unshiu" title="Citrus unshiu">Satsuma</a> (<i>Citrus unshiu</i>), a mandarin × pomelo hybrid with more pomelo than seen in most mandarins.  It derived from a cross between a Huanglingmiao/Kishu and a non-King Kunenbo that was itself a pomelo × Huanglingmiao/Kishu cross.<sup id="cite_ref-Talon_2-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Talon-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Shimizu_32-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Shimizu-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup> It is a seedless variety, of which there are over 200 <a href="/wiki/Cultivar" title="Cultivar">cultivars</a>, including Wenzhou migana, Owari, and mikan; the source of most canned mandarins, and popular as a fresh fruit due to its ease of consumption
<ul><li>Owari, a well-known Satsuma cultivar that ripens during the late autumn</li></ul></li></ul></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Komikan_(fruit)" title="Komikan (fruit)">Komikan</a>, a variety of Kishumikan<sup id="cite_ref-Shimizu_32-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Shimizu-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup></li></ul></li>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/Ponkan" title="Ponkan">Ponkan</a> (<i>Citrus reticulata</i>), a mandarin–pomelo hybrid<sup id="cite_ref-Curk_19-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Curk-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-genealogy_review_29-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-genealogy_review-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup>
<ul><li>The <a href="/wiki/Dancy_tangerine" class="mw-redirect" title="Dancy tangerine">Dancy tangerine</a> (<i>Citrus tangerina</i>) is a hybrid, the cross of a Ponkan with another unidentified hybrid mandarin.<sup id="cite_ref-Talon_2-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Talon-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> Until the 1970s, most tangerines grown and eaten in the US were Dancys, and it was known as "Christmas tangerine"<sup id="cite_ref-arkoftaste_17-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-arkoftaste-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> and zipper-skin tangerine<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Iyokan" title="Iyokan">Iyokan</a> (<i>Citrus iyo</i>), a cross between the Dancy tangerine and another Japanese mandarin variety, the kaikoukan.<sup id="cite_ref-Shimizu_32-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Shimizu-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup></li></ul></li></ul></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Bang_Mot_tangerine" title="Bang Mot tangerine">Bang Mot tangerine</a>, a mandarin variety popular in Thailand.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Shekwasha" class="mw-redirect" title="Shekwasha">Shekwasha</a> (<i>Citrus depressa</i>), a group of clonal citrus that arose from multiple independent natural crosses of <i>C. ryukyuensis</i> with a Sun Chu Sha relative,<sup id="cite_ref-Wu2021_20-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Wu2021-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> a very sour mandarin grown for its acidic juice.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Tachibana_orange" title="Tachibana orange">Tachibana</a>, also a cluster of similar clones, deriving from natural crosses between different individual <i>C. ryukyuensis</i> and a clonal <i>C. reticulata</i> lineage with both northern and southern subspecies contribution.<sup id="cite_ref-Wu2021_20-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Wu2021-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Kinnow" title="Kinnow">Kinnow</a>, also known as Pakistani mandarin is popular variety in Pakistan and Middle East.</li></ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Mandarin_crosses">Mandarin crosses</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mandarin_orange&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Mandarin crosses"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<figure class="mw-halign-right" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Citrus_tern_cb_simplified_1.svg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Citrus_tern_cb_simplified_1.svg/400px-Citrus_tern_cb_simplified_1.svg.png" decoding="async" width="400" height="375" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Citrus_tern_cb_simplified_1.svg/600px-Citrus_tern_cb_simplified_1.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Citrus_tern_cb_simplified_1.svg/800px-Citrus_tern_cb_simplified_1.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="823" data-file-height="771" /></a><figcaption>Citrus fruits clustered by genetic similarity. Most commercial <a href="/wiki/Citrus_taxonomy" title="Citrus taxonomy">varieties of citrus</a> are hybrids of the three species at the corners of the <a href="/wiki/Ternary_diagram" class="mw-redirect" title="Ternary diagram">ternary diagram</a> (mandarin at top). Genetically distinct hybrids often bear the same <a href="/wiki/Folk_taxonomy" title="Folk taxonomy">common name</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-limes_and_lemons_34-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-limes_and_lemons-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup></figcaption></figure>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Tangelo" title="Tangelo">Tangelos</a>, a generic term for modern mandarin (tangerine) × pomelo and mandarin × <a href="/wiki/Grapefruit" title="Grapefruit">grapefruit</a> crosses
<ul><li>The <a href="/wiki/Mandelo" title="Mandelo">Mandelo</a> or 'cocktail grapefruit', a cross between a Dancy/King mixed mandarin and a pomelo.<sup id="cite_ref-Talon_2-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Talon-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> The term is also sometimes used generically, like a tangelo, for recent mandarin × pomelo hybrids.</li></ul></li>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/Sour_orange" class="mw-redirect" title="Sour orange">sour orange</a> (<i>Citrus</i> x <i>aurantium</i>) derives from a direct cross between a pure mandarin and a pomelo<sup id="cite_ref-genealogy_31-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-genealogy-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Lemon" title="Lemon">Lemon</a> (<i>Citrus</i> x <i>limon</i>), a sour orange × <a href="/wiki/Citron" title="Citron">citron</a> hybrid.<sup id="cite_ref-limes_and_lemons_34-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-limes_and_lemons-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Lime_(fruit)" title="Lime (fruit)">Lime</a> (<i>Citrus</i> x <i>latifolia</i>), a lemon × <a href="/wiki/Key_lime" title="Key lime">Key lime</a> cross<sup id="cite_ref-limes_and_lemons_34-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-limes_and_lemons-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Bergamot_orange" title="Bergamot orange">Bergamot orange</a> (<i>Citrus</i> x <i>bergamia</i>), a lemon × sour orange backcross<sup id="cite_ref-limes_and_lemons_34-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-limes_and_lemons-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup></li></ul></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Limetta" class="mw-redirect" title="Limetta">Limetta</a> (<i>Citrus limetta</i>), a distinct sour orange × citron hybrid<sup id="cite_ref-limes_and_lemons_34-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-limes_and_lemons-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup></li></ul></li>
<li>The common <a href="/wiki/Orange_(fruit)" title="Orange (fruit)">sweet orange</a> (<i>Citrus</i> x <i>sinensis</i>) derives from a cross between a non-pure mandarin and pomelo parents<sup id="cite_ref-genealogy_31-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-genealogy-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Tangor" title="Tangor">Tangors</a>, or <i>Temple oranges</i>, are crosses between the mandarin orange and the common sweet orange;<sup id="cite_ref-genealogy_31-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-genealogy-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> their thick <a href="/wiki/Peel_(fruit)" title="Peel (fruit)">rind</a> is easy to peel, and its bright orange pulp is sour-sweet and full-flavoured. Some such hybrids are commonly called mandarins or tangerines.
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Clementine" title="Clementine">Clementine</a> (<i>Citrus</i> × <i>clementina</i>), a spontaneous hybrid between a Willowleaf mandarin orange and a sweet orange.<sup id="cite_ref-genealogy_review_29-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-genealogy_review-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Edible_35-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Edible-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup> sometimes known as a "Thanksgiving Orange" or "Christmas orange", as its peak season is <a href="/wiki/Winter" title="Winter">winter</a>; an important commercial mandarin orange form, having displaced <a href="/wiki/Citrus_unshiu" title="Citrus unshiu">mikans</a> in many markets.
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Clemenules" class="mw-redirect" title="Clemenules">Clemenules</a> or <a href="/wiki/Nules" title="Nules">Nules</a>, a variety of Clementine named for the Valencian town where it was first bred in 1953; it is the most popular variety of Clementine grown in Spain.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Fairchild_(fruit)" class="mw-redirect" title="Fairchild (fruit)">Fairchild</a> is a hybrid of <a href="/wiki/Clementine" title="Clementine">Clementine</a> and <a href="/wiki/Grapefruit#Grapefruit_relatives" title="Grapefruit">Orlando</a> tangelo</li></ul></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Murcott_(fruit)" title="Murcott (fruit)">Murcott</a>, a mandarin × sweet orange hybrid,<sup id="cite_ref-genealogy_review_29-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-genealogy_review-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup> one parent being the King.<sup id="cite_ref-Shimizu_32-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Shimizu-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup>
<ul><li>Tango is a proprietary seedless mid-late season irradiated selection of Murcott developed by the University of California Citrus Breeding Program.<sup id="cite_ref-ucr_8-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ucr-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup></li></ul></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Kiyomi" title="Kiyomi">Kiyomi</a> (<i>Citrus unshiu</i> × <i>sinensis</i>) is a Satsuma/sweet orange hybrid from Japan
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Dekopon" title="Dekopon">Dekopon</a>, a hybrid between Kiyomi and ponkan, marketed in the United States as Sumo Citrus(R)</li></ul></li></ul></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Grapefruit" title="Grapefruit">Grapefruit</a> (<i>Citrus</i> x <i>paradisi</i>), the result of backcrossing the sweet orange with pomelo</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Meyer_lemon" title="Meyer lemon">Meyer lemon</a> (<i>Citrus</i> x <i>meyer</i>), a cross between a mandarin × pomelo hybrid and a <a href="/wiki/Citron" title="Citron">citron</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-limes_and_lemons_34-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-limes_and_lemons-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Palestinian_sweet_lime" title="Palestinian sweet lime">Palestinian sweet lime</a> (<i>Citrus</i> x <i>limettioides</i>), a distinct (mandarin × pomelo) × citron hybrid<sup id="cite_ref-limes_and_lemons_34-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-limes_and_lemons-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup></li></ul></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Rangpur_(fruit)" title="Rangpur (fruit)">Rangpur</a> lime (<i>Citrus</i> x <i>limonia</i>), a pure-mandarin × citron cross<sup id="cite_ref-limes_and_lemons_34-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-limes_and_lemons-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Rough_lemon" title="Rough lemon">Rough lemon</a> (<i>Citrus</i> x <i>jambhiri</i>), a pure-mandarin × citron cross, distinct from rangpur<sup id="cite_ref-limes_and_lemons_34-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-limes_and_lemons-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Volkamer_lemon" title="Volkamer lemon">Volkamer lemon</a> (<i>Citrus volkameriana</i>), a pure-mandarin x <a href="/wiki/Citron" title="Citron">citron</a> cross, distinct from rangpur and rough lemon</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Jabara_(citrus)" title="Jabara (citrus)">Jabara</a> (<i>Citrus jabara</i>), a Kunenbo mandarin × <a href="/wiki/Yuzu" title="Yuzu">yuzu</a> cross.<sup id="cite_ref-Shimizu_32-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Shimizu-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>several of the kumquat-hybrid <i><a href="/wiki/Citrofortunella" title="Citrofortunella">Citrofortunella</a></i>, including <a href="/wiki/Calamansi" title="Calamansi">calamansi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Citrangequat" title="Citrangequat">citrangequat</a>, <a href="/wiki/Orangequat" class="mw-redirect" title="Orangequat">orangequat</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mandarinquat" title="Mandarinquat">mandarinquat</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sunquat" title="Sunquat">sunquat</a></li></ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Non-mandarins">Non-mandarins</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mandarin_orange&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Non-mandarins"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Mangshanyegans" class="mw-redirect" title="Mangshanyegans">Mangshanyegans</a>, long thought to be mandarins, are a separate species.<sup id="cite_ref-genealogy_31-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-genealogy-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mandarin_orange&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: See also"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="References">References</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mandarin_orange&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: References"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
